Resolving Conflict Between Qiyas by Preferring Based on Ḥāl
Explaining the fourth method to resolve conflict between two analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of tarjīh bi al-ḥāl and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position on multiple aqwāl.

Core Idea
When two qiyas conflict, neither is dropped; the mujtahid must prefer based on inner inclination, not external state.

This passage from Khulasat al-Anwar discusses the fourth method of resolving conflict between analogies: preference based on ḥāl. The Hanafi school holds that the mere existence of a conflicting opinion does not invalidate both; rather, the mujtahid must follow his inner conviction. This contrasts with Imam Shafi'i's view that multiple opinions can coexist at the same time. A critical objection about the case of donkey urine (sūr himār) is addressed by the principle of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
Recognize that two qiyas appear to contradict each other in a branch ruling.
Conflict (ta'āruḍ) requires resolution; both cannot be applied simultaneously.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule
Neither qiyas is abandoned; rather, preference (tarjīḥ) becomes obligatory.
The ḥāl (state of being conflicting) is not a proof that drops both.
3
Understand the mechanism of tarjīḥ
The mujtahid relies on his inner inclination (rujhān qalbī), not on the external state alone.
Hanafis require rujhān qalbī for preference; it is not mere whim but arises from deep ijtihad.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Imam Shafi'i does not require inner inclination, thus multiple aqwāl can exist from one mujtahid at the same time.
This leads to a practical difference in the number of relied-upon opinions in each school.
5
Resolve the objection
The case of donkey urine is an exception: Hanafis acted on ḥāl there due to necessity (ḍarūra), which permits normally restricted actions.
Necessity does not elevate ḥāl to a general proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چهارم اگر دو قیاسوں کے درمیان تعارض واقع ہو تو یہ دونوں ساقط نہیں ہو نگے ۔ بلکہ عمل بالحال واجب ہوگا کیونکہ حل یعنی تقریر الاصول ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے ۔ بلکہ مجتہد دونوں متعارض قیاسوں میں سے اپنے قلبی رجحان کی بنیاد پر کسی پر عمل کرلے گا جبکہ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے ہاں رحمان قلبی بھی ضروری نہیں اس لئے ایک ہی وقت میں ان کے ایک اجتہادی مسئلے میں متعدد اقوال بھی ہوتے ہیں۔ جبکہ احناف کا یہ امتیاز ہے کہ ایک وقت میں ان سے دو یا زائد اقوال مروی نہیں۔ اعتراض اگر آپ کے نزدیک حال حجت نہیں تو سور حمار میں آپ نے اس پر عمل کیوں کیا؟ جواب سور حمار کے مسئلے میں اس کو اختیار کرنا ضرورت کی بناء پر ہے والضرورات تبيح المحذورت .
Fourth: If there is conflict between two qiyas, then both are not dropped. Rather, acting according to the state (ḥāl) is obligatory because the state (i.e., the affirmative report? istiqrā' al-uṣūl) is not a proof in our view. Rather, the mujtahid, between the two conflicting qiyas, will act upon the one based on his inner inclination. Whereas according to Imam Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, inner inclination is not necessary; therefore, at one time, multiple statements (aqwāl) are narrated from him in one ijtihād issue. Whereas the Hanafis have the distinction that at one time, two or more statements are not narrated from them. Objection: If in your view the state (ḥāl) is not a proof, then in the matter of donkey urine (sūr himār) why did you act upon it? Answer: In the issue of donkey urine, choosing it is out of necessity, and necessities permit prohibitions.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position on resolving conflict between two qiyas. The Hanafis do not consider the 'state' (ḥāl) or the mere existence of a conflicting opinion as a proof that drops both qiyas; rather, the mujtahid must prefer one based on his inner conviction. Imam Shafi'i allows multiple opinions from one mujtahid at the same time, but the Hanafis do not. The objection about donkey urine is answered by saying that the use of ḥāl there was a necessity (ḍarūra), which permits what would otherwise be prohibited.

Key Terms
حال (ḥāl): The existing state or situation that influences preference between two conflicting qiyas.
رجحان قلبی (rujhān qalbī): Inner inclination of the mujtahid towards one of the conflicting evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi rule when two qiyas conflict, according to this passage?
A) Both qiyas are dropped and a new evidence must be sought
B) The mujtahid follows the qiyas that has stronger external support (ḥāl)
C) The mujtahid prefers one based on his inner inclination (rujhān qalbī)
D) The mujtahid waits for consensus (ijmā') to resolve the conflict

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conflict between two qiyas does not nullify them; preference is made through the mujtahid's inner inclination, not the external state of conflict.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Dispute on the 'Iddah of a Pregnant Widow: Ali vs. Ibn Mas'ud
Explaining the ikhtilaf between Ali and Ibn Mas'ud on the 'iddah of a pregnant widow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of naskh to reconcile conflicting Quranic verses and evaluate the ikhtilaf between Ali (RA) and Ibn Mas'ud (RA) on the 'iddah of a pregnant widow.

Core Idea
When Quranic verses conflict, naskh (abrogation) based on revelation order takes precedence over reconciling by taking the later term.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute between two great Companions: Ali (RA) and Ibn Mas'ud (RA). Both were confronted with the case of a woman who is both pregnant and widowed. The Quran provides two relevant verses: one in Surah al-Baqarah stating four months and ten days for a widow, and another in Surah al-Talaq stating that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends at delivery. The disagreement centers on whether the later verse abrogates the earlier one (Ibn Mas'ud) or whether we must reconcile by taking the longer of the two terms (Ali). The Hanafi school follows Ibn Mas'ud, relying on historical knowledge of revelation order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Quranic verses and their apparent conflict
Recall Surah al-Baqarah 2:234 (widow's 'iddah is 4 months 10 days) and Surah al-Talaq 65:4 (pregnant woman's 'iddah is delivery). The conflict arises when a woman is both pregnant and widowed.
These verses individually are clear, but apply to the same person simultaneously.
2
Understand Ali's position and his rationale
Ali (RA) argues that we do not know which verse was revealed first, so we cannot claim naskh. Instead, we must reconcile by making her 'iddah the later of the two terms (ab'adul ajalayn).
This is a cautious approach based on uncertainty.
3
Understand Ibn Mas'ud's position and his evidence
Ibn Mas'ud (RA) asserts that Surah al-Talaq was revealed after Surah al-Baqarah, thus it abrogates the earlier verse for the combined case. He used to challenge others to ask him about the 'short surah of women' (Surah al-Talaq).
He relies on transmitted knowledge (riwayah) of revelation order.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle of naskh
Accepting Ibn Mas'ud's historical claim, the later verse (65:4) abrogates the earlier (2:234) for pregnant widows. Therefore, the 'iddah is only delivery.
Naskh is established when a later revealed text overrules an earlier one on the same subject.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Ali's view, a pregnant widow might wait up to 10 months if delivery occurs after 4 months 10 days. Under Ibn Mas'ud's view, she is free to remarry as soon as she delivers, which could be much sooner.
The difference affects the woman's ability to remarry and financial support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامہ ملاجیون رحمہ اللہ کی تشریح دل پزیر فرماتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں آنتوں کے درمیان عموم خصوص من وجہ کی نسبت ہے جس میں کل تین ماہ ہوتے ہیں ۔ دو مادے افتراقی اور ایک اجتماعی مادہ ۔ یہاں بھی دو افتراقی مادے ہیں ۔ اور ایک اجتماعی مادہ۔ (۱) اجتماعی مادہ: وہ عورت جو حاملہ بھی ہو اور متوفی عنھا زوجھا بھی ہو (۲) افتراقی مادہ اولی: وہ عورت جو حاملہ ہو مگر متوفی عنھا زوجھا نہ ہو۔ (۳) افتراقی مادہ ثانیہ: وہ عورت جو متوفی عنھا زوجھا ہو لیکن حاملہ نہ ہو افتراقی مادوں میں کوئی اشکال نہیں لہذا متوفی عنھا زوجھا ( فقط) کی عدت چار ماہ دس دن قرار پائے گی ۔ کما فی آیت البقرۃ اور حاملہ (فقط) کی عدت وضع حمل قرار پائے گی کما فی آیت الطلاق البتہ پریشانی اجتماعی مادے کی صورت میں لاحق ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اس عورت کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں آیا اسے متوفى عنها زوجها قرار دیں یا حاملہ ۔ شارح رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے یہاں فقہاء صحابہ حضرت علی اور حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعودرضی اللہ تعالی عنہما کا اختلاف نقل کیا ہے۔ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کا مذهب خلیفہ رابع حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایسی عورت ابعد الاجلین عدت گزارے یعنی دیکھا جائے کہ وضع حمل چار ماہ دس دن سے قبل ہوتا ہے یا بعد میں ۔ اگر پہلے ہو تو چار ماہ دس دن کا انتظار کرے اور اگر بعد میں ہوتو ۴ ماہ دس دن گذرنے کے بعد بھی بیٹھی رہے یہاں تک کہ وضع حمل ہو جائے ۔ حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود کا مذھب ایسی عورت کی عدت فقط وضع حمل ہے حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کا عذر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمیں معلوم نہیں کہ سورہ بقرہ والی آیت پہلے ہے یا سورۃ الطلاق والی ۔ لہذا تاریخ معلوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہم کسی کو تاریخ اور کسی کو منسوخ قرار نہیں دے سکتے اور تطبیق والی یہی صورت ہے کہ ابعد الاجلین کو اسکی عدت قرار دیا جائے ۔ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کا موقف: وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سورۃ البقرہ والی آیت منسوخ ہے کیونکہ سورۃ الطلاق والی آیت اس کے بعد اتری ہے انکا چیلنج تھا فرمایا کرتے تھے من شاء با هلته سورة النساء القصرى أعنى سورة الطلاق التي فيها وأولات الأحمال الخ نزلت بعد التي في سورة البقرة نکتہ ائمہ مجتہدین میں سے امام ابوحنیفہ، امام شافعی، اور جمہور صحابہ وتابعین رحیم اللہ کا سلفاً عن خلف مذھب حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود اور حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہما کے موافق ہے۔
Mulla Mulla Jiyun's commentary pleasing to the heart says: Between these two intestines there is a relation of general-particular from one aspect, which has three total aspects: two individual materials and one social material. Here also there are two individual materials and one social material. (1) Social material: the woman who is both pregnant and her husband has died. (2) First individual material: the woman who is pregnant but not widowed. (3) Second individual material: the woman who is widowed but not pregnant. In the individual materials there is no problem: therefore the 'iddah of the widowed (only) is four months and ten days, as in the verse of al-Baqarah; and the 'iddah of the pregnant (only) is delivery, as in the verse of al-Talaq. However, difficulty arises in the case of the social material because this woman has two aspects: should we consider her as a widow or as pregnant? The commentator (may Allah's mercy be upon him) has transmitted here the ikhtilaf of the jurist companions: Ali and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with them both). The madhhab of Ali (RA): The fourth caliph Ali (RA) says that such a woman should observe the later of the two terms, i.e., see whether delivery occurs before four months and ten days or after. If earlier, then she waits four months and ten days; if later, then after four months and ten days pass, she remains until delivery. The madhhab of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA): The 'iddah of such a woman is only delivery. Ali's excuse: He says: We do not know whether the verse in Surah al-Baqarah came first or the one in Surah al-Talaq. Therefore, due to unknown history, we cannot declare one abrogated and the other abrogator, and the only reconciling approach is to make her 'iddah the later of the two terms. The position of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA): He says that the verse of Surah al-Baqarah is abrogated because the verse of Surah al-Talaq was revealed after it. He used to challenge: Whoever wishes, let him ask me about the short Surah of Women, meaning Surah al-Talaq, in which is 'And those who are pregnant...' it was revealed after the one in Surah al-Baqarah. Note: Among the imams of ijtihad, Imam Abu Hanifah, Imam al-Shafi'i, and the majority of the Companions and Successors (may Allah's mercy be upon them) successively follow the madhhab of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Umar (RA).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul dispute from the Hanafi tradition concerning the 'iddah of a woman who is both pregnant and widowed. The author first categorizes the scenarios: social material (both characteristics) and two individual materials (only one each). For the individual cases, there is consensus: the widow's 'iddah is four months and ten days (Quran 2:234), and the pregnant woman's 'iddah is delivery (Quran 65:4). The dispute arises for the combined case. Ali (RA) argues for the later of the two terms (ab court al-ajlayn) because he cannot determine which verse was revealed first, so he reconciles by giving both effects. Ibn Mas'ud (RA) argues that the verse from Surah al-Talaq abrogates the earlier verse from Surah al-Baqarah, making delivery alone sufficient. The author concludes that the majority of scholars, including Imams Abu Hanifah and al-Shafi'i, follow the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud and Umar (RA), which is also the relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying.
وضع حمل (wad' haml): Delivery of the baby; the end of pregnancy.
ابعد الاجلین (ab'adul ajalayn): The later of the two terms (four months ten days or delivery).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the 'iddah of a woman who is both pregnant and widowed?
A) Four months and ten days regardless of delivery.
B) Only until delivery.
C) The later of delivery or four months and ten days.
D) A total of one year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that a pregnant widow's 'iddah ends at delivery is based on naskh: the later Quranic verse (65:4) abrogates the earlier (2:234) for the combined case.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
The Rule of Preferred Affirmation: The Case of Mughith
Applies the rule of preferred affirmation to the dispute over Mughith's slave status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to APPLY the Hanafi usul rule that affirming evidence (muthbit) is preferred over negating evidence (nafi) to resolve a hadith-based ikhtilaf, and IDENTIFY the thamarah al-khilaf in the marriage option (khiyar) for a freed slave woman.

Core Idea
When two reports conflict, the one that affirms a fact based on direct evidence takes precedence over the one that denies it based on a presumption.

The hadith of Barirah presents a classic usul dispute: Was Barirah's husband Mughith free or slave when she was given the choice to stay with him or leave? Imam al-Shafi'i argued that Mughith remained a slave based on the original state (istishab), while the Hanafis argued that he had become free based on an affirming report. This lesson walks through the Hanafi application of the principle that affirming evidence (muthbit) is given precedence over negating evidence (nafi). Understanding this principle is essential for evaluating conflicting reports in hadith and deriving correct rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Determine the factual question at the heart of the dispute – was Mughith free or slave when Barirah was given khiyar?
This is not a dispute about the ruling of khiyar itself, but about the factual status of the husband.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school holds that Mughith was free, so Barirah's option is absolute, regardless of her husband's status.
3
State the Opposing Position
The Shafi'i school holds that Mughith remained a slave, so Barirah's option only applies if her husband is a slave; if he is free, no option.
4
Analyze the Evidence
Contrast the evidence: the affirming report (that Mughith was free) is based on direct knowledge by a narrator, while the negating report (that he was still a slave) is inferred from the original state (istishab) without direct evidence.
The source text states: 'جس راوی نے ان کے حر ہونے کی خبر دی ہے اس نے کسی دلیل کی بنیاد پر دی ہوگی' (The narrator who reported his freedom must have based it on some evidence).
5
Apply the Rule of Preferred Affirmation
The affirming report is given precedence because it is based on evidence, not presumption. This yields the Hanafi ruling: the freed woman always has the option of khiyar upon emancipation, regardless of her husband's status.
The commentator emphasizes that the negating report does not conflict with the affirming report because it is based on the apparent state, not specific knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) النفي في حديث بريره: حدیث بریرہ رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنھا سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ان کے آقاؤں سے خرید کر حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالی عنھا نے آزاد کر دیا تھا جبکہ ان کے شوہر حضرت مغیث رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ غلام تھے ان کو حضور اکرم اللہ نے اختیار دیا کہ چاہے تو حضرت مغیث کے ساتھ زندگی بسر کرلے ورنہ علیحدگی اختیار کرلے ملکت بضعک فاختاری اس تغیر کے وقت حضرت مغیث آزاد تھے یا غلام ؟ ہمیں اختلاف ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا مذھب: حضرت مغیث رضی اللہ تعالٰی بدستور غلام تھے لہذا معتقہ کے لئے خیار اسی صورت میں ثابت ہوگا جب اس کا شوہر غلام ہو ورنہ نہیں۔ حضرات احناف رحمہم اللہ کا مذھب: حضرت مغیث اس وقت آزاد ہو چکے تھے لہذا معتقہ کو ہر صورت میں خیار حاصل ہے خواہ شوہر آزاد ہو یا غلام۔ شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ حریت دارالاسلام میں اصل ہے اور اس پر روایات متفق ہیں کہ حضرت مغیث رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ فی الحقیقت غلام تھے۔ اور اختلاف حریت عارض ہے اب عبودیت کی خبر حریت عارضی کے منافی ہے اور حریت کی خبر ثبت ہے امر عارضی کیلئے۔ جن رواۃ نے یہ کہا کہ كان عبدا فی الاصل یہ ظاہر حال پر ہے کیونکہ پہلے غلام تھے تو شاید اب بھی غلام ہی ہو نگے لہذا خبر نانی مثبت کے معارض نہیں ہوگی (جیسا کہ شوافع نے فرمایا ہے)۔ مذهب احناف کی وجہ ترجیح: ہم حریت کا قول اسلئے کرتے ہیں کہ جس راوی نے ان کے حر ہونے کی خبر دی ہے اس نے کسی دلیل کی بنیاد پر دی ہوگی لہذا ہم مثبت پر عمل کرتے ہیں۔
(1) The negation in the hadith of Barirah: The hadith of Barirah (may Allah be pleased with her) means that Lady Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) bought her from her masters and freed her, while her husband Mughith (may Allah be pleased with him) was a slave. The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave her the choice: either to continue living with Mughith or to separate, saying 'Your ownership of your private part, so choose.' At that time, was Mughith free or a slave? There is disagreement. Imam Shafi'i's school: Mughith was still a slave, so the option for the freed woman is only established if her husband is a slave, otherwise not. The Hanafi school: Mughith had become free by that time, so the freed woman has the option in all cases, whether the husband is free or slave. The commentator says: Freedom is the original state in Dar al-Islam, and the narratives agree that Mughith was in fact a slave. And the difference (between reports) is that freedom is incidental. Now the report of slavery contradicts the incidental freedom, and the report of freedom is established for the incidental matter. Those narrators who said 'he was a slave originally' based it on the apparent state because he was a slave before, so perhaps he is still a slave. Therefore the negating report does not conflict with the affirming report (as the Shafi'is have stated). The reason for preference of the Hanafi school: We adopt the report of freedom because the narrator who reported his freedom must have based it on some evidence; therefore we act on the affirming evidence.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This is an application of the rule from the previous lesson. The dispute is whether Mughith was free or slave when Barirah was given the option of khayr (choice). The Shafi'i argue based on the original state (istishab) that he remained a slave, so the confirming evidence that he was free is not accepted because the original state is stronger. The Hanafi argue that the report of freedom is based on direct evidence, so it takes precedence over the presumption of slavery. The commentator clarifies that the Shafi'i's report of his being a slave originally is based on the apparent state, not on specific knowledge, so it is not considered strong evidence. Thus the Hanafi position is that the affirming report (that he was free) is preferred, consistent with the principle 'العمل بالدليل المثبت أولى'.

Key Terms
خیار (Khiyar): The option given to a slave woman upon emancipation to retain or dissolve her marriage.
معتقہ (Mu'taqah): The female slave who has been emancipated.
حریت (Hurriyah): Freedom as a legal status opposed to slavery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the report that Mughith was free preferred over the report that he was a slave?
A) Because freedom is the original state of humans.
B) Because the report of freedom is based on direct evidence, while the report of slavery is based on istishab.
C) Because the majority of narrators reported freedom.
D) Because the Prophet explicitly stated that Mughith was free.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that affirming evidence (muthbit) is preferred over negating evidence (nafi) ensures that rulings are based on direct knowledge rather than presumption, as illustrated by the resolution of the ikhtilaf over Mughith's status in the hadith of Barirah.

Applying the Rule of Preferring Affirming Evidence: The Case of Maymunah
Applies the rule of preferring affirmation to the dispute over breaking ihram for marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that affirming evidence is preferred over negating evidence to resolve a dispute about a Prophetic action.

Core Idea
When two reports conflict, the affirming report is preferred because it adds knowledge.

This lesson applies a key Hanafi usul principle: when there is a report that the Prophet did something and another that he did not, the affirming report is given priority. We examine the famous case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while in ihram. The dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools hinges on whether marriage is valid during ihram, and which report carries more weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting reports
One report states the Prophet married Maymunah while in ihram (affirming he remained in ihram). Another report states he broke his ihram before the marriage (negating he remained in ihram).
2
Understand the opposing schools' positions
The Shafi'i school holds that marriage is invalid during ihram, so the Prophet must have broken ihram. The Hanafi school holds that marriage is valid during ihram, so he could have remained in ihram.
The disagreement is rooted in different rulings on marriage for a muhrim.
3
Apply the rule of preferring the affirming report
Hanafi usul states that when there is an affirming report (muthbit) and a negating report (nafi), the affirming report is given precedence because it provides additional information beyond the original state.
The rule is: al-`amal bi al-dalil al-muthbit awla (preferring the affirming evidence).
4
Recognize the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The Hanafi ruling allows a muhrim to contract marriage; the Shafi'i ruling prohibits it. This difference affects many fiqh cases.
5
Identify the basis of preference
The affirming report is based on direct witness of the marriage occurring while the Prophet was in ihram. The negating report is based on an inference from the ruling that marriage is invalid during ihram.
The affirming report is more direct and thus stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) النفى في حديث ميمونة رضي الله عنها: حضور اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مقام سرف پر حضرت میمونہ رضی اللہ عنھا سے نکاح کیا تھا نکاح سے قبل آپ بالاتفاق حالت احرام میں تھے آیا حین النکاح آپ نے احرام توڑا یا نہیں اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا مذھب: آپ نے احرام توڑ لیا تھا کیونکہ محرم کے لئے عقد نکاح جائز نہیں۔ امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا مذھب: آپ حالت احرام ہی میں رہے کیونکہ ہمارے ہاں محرم کے لئے احرام میں نکاح جائز ہے البتہ ولی جائز نہیں۔ شارح رحمتہ اللہ علیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ احرام بنی آدم کیلئے اصل نہیں بلکہ عارض ہے لیکن رواۃ کا اتفاق ہے کہ حضور اکرم اس وقت حالت احرام میں تھے۔ اختلاف بین النکاح اس کے باقی رکھنے اور توڑنے میں ہے یہاں میں النکاح محرم ہونے کی خبر نافی ہے اور تنقض احرام کی خبر مثبت۔
(2) The negation in the hadith of Maymunah (may Allah be pleased with her): The Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah at a place called Sarif. Before the marriage, he was in a state of ihram by consensus. Did he break his ihram at the time of marriage or not? There is disagreement. Imam Shafi'i's school: He broke his ihram because a marriage contract is not permissible for a muhrim. Imam Abu Hanifa's school: He remained in ihram because, in our school, marriage is permissible for a muhrim, though being a guardian is not. The commentator says: Ihram for the children of Adam is not original but is incidental. However, the narrators agree that the Prophet was in ihram at that time. The dispute is about whether he maintained or broke it. Here, the report that he married while in ihram (i.e., did not break it) is the affirming report, and the report that he broke ihram is the negating report.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This is another application of the rule. The dispute is about whether the Prophet broke his ihram to marry Maymunah. The Shafi'i argue that marriage is invalid during ihram, so the Prophet must have broken it. The Hanafi argue that marriage is valid during ihram in their school, so the Prophet remained in ihram. The commentator notes that ihram is a temporary state, not an original one. Since the narrators agree that the Prophet was in ihram, the affirming report (that he did not break it) is given preference over the negating report (that he broke it) because the affirming report is based on evidence that the marriage occurred in ihram, while the negating report relies on the assumption that marriage requires breaking ihram. Consistent with the rule 'العمل بالدليل المثبت أولى'.

Key Terms
احرام (Ihram): A sacred state entered for Hajj or Umrah, with certain prohibitions.
نکاح (Nikah): Marriage contract.
عارض (Arid): Incidental, not permanent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Prophet broke his ihram before marriage.
B) The Prophet remained in ihram because marriage is permissible for a muhrim in the Hanafi school.
C) The Prophet was not in ihram at all.
D) The Prophet broke his ihram after marriage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule preferring affirming evidence over negating evidence resolves the dispute about the Prophet's ihram at the time of his marriage to Maymunah, leading to the ruling that a muhrim can contract marriage.

Four Invalid Grounds for Tarjih
Lists four invalid grounds for tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four situations where tarjih is not granted in Hanafi usul and apply the rule that only mutawatir/mashhur over khabar wahid, addition, and certain other substantive grounds are valid for preference.

Core Idea
Tarjih is not granted for number, gender, or freedom status of narrators—only substantive evidence wins.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text clarifies what does NOT give preference between conflicting hadiths. It warns against relying on mere quantity of narrators, their gender, or their social status. Understanding these invalid grounds protects the student from common errors in tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four invalid grounds
Read the passage and list the four situations where preference is explicitly denied: (1) more narrators alone, (2) male narrators over female, (3) free narrators over slaves, (4) automatic preference when one side has two narrators unless it is mutawatir or mashhur.
The fourth point is nuanced: two narrators do not automatically beat one; only if the two-narrator hadith is mutawatir/mashhur does it prevail over khabar wahid.
2
Distinguish valid vs. invalid quantity-based tarjih
Contrast the invalid ‘more narrators’ rule with the valid exception: when one side is khabar wahid (one narrator) and the other is mutawatir or mashhur (many), the latter is preferred. This is because mutawatir gives certainty, not just quantity.
The passage cites al-Mabsut: 'preferring the statement of two over one' in that specific context.
3
Recognize the addition rule
If a single narrator transmits two versions of a hadith, the version with an addition (ziyada) is preferred, provided it does not contradict the other version. Example: Ibn Mas'ud's hadith with the phrase 'and the commodity is present'.
This rule applies within the narrations of one narrator, not between two different narrators.
4
Apply the rules to a hypothetical conflict
Given two conflicting hadiths, first check if either is mutawatir/mashhur over the other. If both are khabar wahid, do not prefer based on number, gender, or freedom. Then look for additions, chain strength, or other substantive factors.
The passage concludes the discussion of ta'arud; this is the last rule before moving on.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والترجيح لا يقع
(1) جس حدیث کے راوی زیادہ ہوں اسے ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوگی ۔
لیکن اگر ایک طرف ایک راوی ہو یعنی وہ حدیث خبر واحد ہو اور دوسری طرف دو یا زائد یعنی وہ خبر متواتر یا مشہور ہو تو اسکو خبر واحد پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی کما قال مح.. رحمة الله عليه ہوتو اسکوخبر
في المبسوط و هو ترجيح قول الاثنين على الواحد (۲) جس حدیث کے راوی مرد ہوں تو اسے اس حدیث پر ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوگی جس کی رادی عورت ہو كحديث عائشه رضي الله عنها -
(۳) اگر ایک متعارض حدیث کے راوی آزاد اور دوسری کے غلام ہوں تو راوی کے آزاد ہونے کی
وجہ سےاسے ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوگی ک حدیث بلال رضى الله تعالى عنه - (۴) اگر ایک راوی سے دو حدیثیں مروں میں آریا تو دونوں کا مضمون ایک ہوگا یا ایک میں کچھ زیادتی ہوگی یا دونوں کا مضمون مختلف ہوگا ۔ اگر ایک یں کچھ زیادتی ہے جیسا کہ ابن مسعود رضی اللہ
تعالی کی حدیث میں والسلعة قائمة کی زیادتی ہے تو یہی زیادتی راج ہو گی ۔
بحمد الله تعارض کی بحث اختتام کو پہنچی ہے
He said: And preference does not occur. (1) A hadith whose narrators are many does not get preference. But if one side has one narrator, i.e., that hadith is khabar wahid, and the other side has two or more, i.e., that is mutawatir or mashhur, then it gets preference over khabar wahid, as said by Muh... may Allah have mercy on him. So it is like [the rule] in al-Mabsut: it is preferring the statement of two over one. (2) A hadith whose narrators are men does not get preference over a hadith whose narrator is a woman, like the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her). (3) If one conflicting hadith has narrators who are free men and the other has slaves, then preference is not granted due to the narrators being free, like the hadith of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him). (4) If two hadiths are narrated from one narrator, then either their content is the same, or one has an addition, or their content is different. If one has an addition, like the addition 'and the commodity is present' in the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him), then this addition is preferred. Praise be to Allah, the discussion of conflict has concluded.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage states rules for preference (tarjih) between conflicting hadiths. It is from a Hanafi usul text. The author clarifies that a larger number of narrators alone does not automatically give preference; only if the one side is khabar wahid and the other is mutawatir or mashhur does the latter prevail. Gender (male vs female narrator) and freedom status (free vs slave) are not grounds for tarjih. Additionally, if a single narrator transmits two versions, the version with an addition (ziyada) is preferred if it does not contradict the other. The passage concludes the discussion of ta'arud (conflict). This reflects the Hanafi approach that tarjih is based on substantive grounds, not mere quantity or social status.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): In this passage, tarjih is the process of preferring one evidence over another when they conflict; it is not granted based solely on number, gender, or freedom status of narrators.
خبر واحد (khabar wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or few narrators, as opposed to mutawatir or mashhur.
متواتر (mutawātir): A hadith narrated by so many narrators at each level that it is impossible they colluded in lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does NOT give preference to a hadith?
A) The hadith being mutawatir over a khabar wahid
B) The narrators being male over female
C) The addition of extra words in a narration
D) The narrators being free men over slaves

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in Hanafi usul is not based on gender, freedom status, or mere number of narrators, but on substantive grounds like certainty level and textual additions.

When Can the Quran Be Modified? Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Khabar Wahid and Qiyas
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on khabar wahid and qiyas modifying Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the authority of khabar wahid and qiyas relative to the Quran, and evaluate the practical consequences (thamarah) of this disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Only certain (qat'i) evidence can change the Quran; khabar wahid and qiyas, being zanni, lack that authority.

One of the most consequential disputes in usul al-fiqh is whether a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) or analogical reasoning (qiyas) can restrict or add to a clear Quranic ruling. The Hanafi school holds that only reports that are mutawatir or mashhur—those that impart certainty—can modify the Quran. The Shafi'i school, by contrast, accepts khabar wahid and qiyas as valid sources for such specification. This lesson unpacks the dispute, examines the reasoning on both sides, and traces the practical differences through two classic examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Usul Issue
State the exact point of disagreement: Can a khabar wahid (solitary report) or qiyas (analogy) change (takhsis or abrogate) a general or specific Quranic ruling?
The issue turns on the epistemological status of Quranic texts (qat'i) vs. other sources (zanni).
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Proof
The Hanafi school holds that only mutawatir and mashhur reports—which convey certainty—can modify the Quran. Khabar wahid and qiyas are speculative (zanni) and cannot override certain texts.
The Quranic text itself is qat'i al-thubut; a zanni dalil cannot abrogate or specify it.
3
State the Shafi'i Position and Its Proof
The Shafi'i school argues that the Prophet's statements (even solitary ones) and qiyas are valid tools for explaining and specifying the Quran. They cite the hadith on exile for unmarried fornicators as an example.
Shafi'is see the Sunnah as an independent source of legislation that can clarify the Quran.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Hanafis respond that khabar wahid can supplement or explain only where it does not contradict a clear Quranic text. In cases of conflict, the Quranic text prevails. Qiyas is even weaker and cannot restrict a mutlaq (unrestricted) command.
The Hanafi response is grounded in the hierarchy of sources: Quran > Sunnah (mutawatir/mashhur) > khabar wahid > qiyas.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical ruling differences. For the hadd of an unmarried fornicator: Hanafi = 100 lashes only; Shafi'i = 100 lashes + one year exile. For kaffarah: Hanafi accepts any slave; Shafi'i requires a believing slave.
These examples show how a theoretical usul dispute translates into divergent fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے ہاں یہ صرف خبر متواتر اور خبر مشہور کے ذریعے جائز ہے۔ کتاب اللہ کے خصوص یا عموم کو تبدیل کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی۔ جبکہ شوافع کے ہاں یہ خبر واحد سے بھی جائز ہے اور قیاس سے بھی۔
ثمرۃ اختلاف کی مثالوں سے وضاحت
مثال: -------- کتاب اللہ میں غیر محصن زانیہ اور زانی کی سزا ہے: "فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة" اب ہمارے ہاں اسے خبر واحد سے تبدیل نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ جس میں سو کوڑوں کے ساتھ ایک سالہ جلاوطنی بھی آئی ہے کما قال عليه الصلوة والسلام: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة و تعزيب عام" شوافع کے ہاں جائز ہے یہ مثال ہے خبر واحد کی۔
مثال: -------- قرآن مجید میں کفارہ یمین اور کفارہ ظہار میں آزاد کرنے کیلئے غلام کا مسلمان ہونا شرط نہیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان میں صرف "تحرير رقبة" مذکور ہے۔ جبکہ شوافع ان کو کفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے غلام کے مسلمان ہونے کی قید لگاتے ہیں کیونکہ وہاں "تحرير رقبة مؤمنة" کی قید ہے لہذ البقیہ کفاروں کو کفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے ان کے لئے بھی غلام کے مؤمن ہونے کی قید لگاتے ہیں۔
The fruit of the disagreement is that according to us (Hanafis) this is only permissible through mutawatir and mashhur reports. It does not have the ability to change the specific or general of the Book of Allah. While according to the Shafi'is, it is permissible through khabar wahid and also through qiyas.
Clarification with examples of the fruit of disagreement:
Example: In the Book of Allah, the punishment for the unmarried male and female fornicator is: "So flog each one of them one hundred lashes." According to us, this cannot be changed by khabar wahid, in which there is also a year of exile along with the hundred lashes, as he (peace be upon him) said: "The virgin with the virgin, one hundred lashes and exile for a year." According to the Shafi'is it is permissible. This is an example of khabar wahid.
Example: In the noble Qur'an, for the expiation of an oath and the expiation of zihar, it is not a condition that the slave be Muslim when freeing, because in the command of Allah Almighty only "freeing a neck" is mentioned. While the Shafi'is, by analogizing them to the expiation of killing, impose the condition of the slave being Muslim, because there the condition of "a believing neck" is present. Therefore, they analogize the remaining expiations to the expiation of killing and impose the condition of the slave being believing for them as well.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage explains the practical outcome (thamarah) of a fundamental usul difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the power of khabar wahid (solitary report) and qiyas (analogy) to limit or abrogate the general or specific rulings of the Quran. The Hanafi position, as stated here, is that only mutawatir and mashhur narrations—which carry certainty—can modify a clear Quranic text. Khabar wahid and qiyas, being speculative, have no such authority. This is illustrated with two examples. First, the Quranic hadd for unmarried fornicators is one hundred lashes (Quran 24:2). A hadith adds a year of exile. Hanafis reject this addition as it is based on khabar wahid, whereas Shafi'is accept it. Second, the Quran mentions 'freeing a slave' for kaffarah without specifying faith, but Shafi'is analogize to the expiation for accidental killing (where 'believing slave' is required) and thus require a Muslim slave for all kaffarat. Hanafis reject this qiyas as it would alter the clear text.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur or shuhrah, thus providing only speculative knowledge.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared cause (illah).
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators in every generation, making its truth certain.
مشہور (mashhur): A report that is well-known among the scholars, though not reaching the level of tawatur; for Hanafis, it is considered to yield certainty (ilm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as expressed in this passage, what type of report can change the general or specific ruling of the Quran?
A) Any authentic hadith
B) Only mutawatir and mashhur reports
C) Khabar wahid if it is strong
D) Qiyas supported by consensus

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits modification of the Quran only by mutawatir or mashhur reports; khabar wahid and qiyas are too speculative to override a certain text.

Legal Status of Previous Revealed Laws (Shara'i' Man Qablana)
Dispute on bindingness of previous prophetic laws

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on shara'i' man qablana and apply the Hanafi criterion of nakir to determine whether a previous law is binding on Muslims.

Core Idea
A previous prophetic law binds Muslims unless the Quran or Sunnah explicitly disapproves of it.

This passage addresses a fundamental question in usul al-fiqh: are the laws of earlier prophets binding on the Muslim community? The answer is not a simple yes or no. Three views exist, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that such laws are binding only when they are narrated in Islamic sources without expression of disapproval (nakir). This nuanced approach allows the final shari'ah to supersede earlier ones while retaining compatible rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
Recognize that the passage discusses shara'i' man qablana – laws revealed to prophets before Prophet Muhammad (saw).
2
Enumerate the three positions
List the three views: absolutely binding, absolutely non-binding, and the majority (jumhur) position that it depends on the presence or absence of nakir.
3
Understand the majority criterion
Grasp that the key criterion is nakir – explicit disapproval in Quran or Sunnah. If present, the law is not binding; if absent, it is binding.
4
Analyze the examples
See how qisas, water distribution, and prohibition of sodomy are binding because they are narrated without disapproval. Jewish dietary restrictions are non-binding because they are explicitly described as punishment.
5
Trace the dalil naqli
Note that the evidence comes from Quranic verses – both those that mention previous laws neutrally and those that indicate abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وشرائع من قبلنا اذا قص الله ورسوله من غير انكار ایک معرکة الآراء مسئلے کا بیان۔ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی بعثت کے بعد تمام سابقہ شریعتیں منسوخ ہوئیں اب شرائع سابقہ پر عمل کرنے کا کیا حکم ہے؟ اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ (۱) بعض علماء کا مذہب شرائع سابقہ پر عمل واجب ہے مطلقاً (۲) بعض دیگر علماء کا مذہب شرائع سابقہ پر عمل کرنا واجب نہیں مطلقاً۔ (۳) جمہور علماء کا مذہب رائج مذہب یہ ہے کہ دیکھا جائے گا اگر شرائع سابقہ کے ان احکام پر نکیر وارد ہوئی ہے خواہ قرآن میں ہو یا حدیث میں تو یہ ہمارے لئے واجب العمل نہیں لیکن اگر ان کا ذکر قرآن یا حدیث میں آیا ہے اور ان پر اللہ تعالیٰ اور رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کوئی نکیر نہیں فرمائی تو وہ ہمارے لئے واجب العمل ہیں۔ چند مثالیں ان احکام سابقہ کی جو ہم پر واجب ہیں (1) قصاص کا قانون: یہ حکم بنی اسرائیل پر اترا تھا جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے: وَكَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهَا أَنَّ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالْعَيْنَ بِالْعَيْنِ وَالْأَنْفَ بِالْأَنْفِ وَالْأُذُنَ بِالْأُذُنِ وَالسِّنَّ بِالسِّنِّ وَالْجُرُوحَ قِصَاصٌ (۲) باری مقرر کرنا: سب سے پہلے حضرت صالح علیہ السلام نے اپنی اونٹنی کے متعلق قوم کی باریاں مقرر کی تھیں۔ كما قال الله تعالى: وَنَبِّئْهُمْ أَنَّ الْمَاءَ قِسْمَةٌ بَيْنَهُمْ (۳) لواطت کی حرمت: قال تعالى: أَئِنَّكُمْ لَتَأْتُونَ الرِّجَالَ شَهْوَةً دُونَ النِّسَاءِ۔ چند مثالیں ان احکام سابقہ کی جو بوجہ نکیر ہم پر حجت نہیں (۱) یہود پر ناخن والے جانور، گائے اور بھیڑ بکریوں کی چربی حرام تھیں ہم پر حلال ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ حرمت ان پر بطور سزا کے تھی كما قال تعالى: وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ هَادُوا حَرَّمْنَا كُلَّ ذِي ظُفُرٍ وَمِنَ الْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ حَرَّمْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ شُحُومَهُمَا ذَلِكَ جَزَيْنَاهُمْ بِبَغْيِهِمْ۔ الخ
His statement: 'And laws of those before us' when Allah and His Messenger relate them without disapproval is a statement of a point of contention. After the Prophet's (peace be upon him) sending, all previous shari'ahs were abrogated. Now what is the ruling on acting upon previous shari'ahs? There is disagreement. (1) Some scholars hold that acting upon previous shari'ahs is absolutely obligatory. (2) Some other scholars hold that acting upon previous shari'ahs is absolutely not obligatory. (3) The majority of scholars, the prevalent view, is that we consider: if disapproval (nakir) is expressed regarding those rulings of previous shari'ahs, whether in the Quran or Hadith, then they are not binding upon us. But if they are mentioned in the Quran or Hadith and Allah and His Messenger did not express any disapproval, then they are binding upon us. Some examples of previous rulings that are obligatory upon us: (1) The law of qisas (retaliation): This ruling was sent down to the Children of Israel, as Allah says: 'And We prescribed for them therein: life for life, eye for eye, nose for nose, ear for ear, tooth for tooth, and retaliation for wounds.' (2) Apportioning turns: Prophet Salih (peace be upon him) first apportioned turns for his she-camel with his people, as Allah says: 'And inform them that the water is divided between them.' (3) Prohibition of sodomy: Allah says: 'Indeed, you approach men with desire instead of women.' Some examples of previous rulings that are not binding upon us due to disapproval: (1) For the Jews, animals with claws, and the fat of cows and sheep were forbidden; for us they are lawful. Because that prohibition was a punishment for them, as Allah says: 'And to those who Judaized We forbade every animal with claws; and of the cattle and sheep We forbade to them their fat; that We recompensed them for their transgression.' ... etc.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage addresses a foundational usul al-fiqh issue: the hukm of shara'i' man qablana (laws of previous prophets). The author presents three positions: one extreme views them as absolutely binding, another as absolutely non-binding, and the jumhur (majority) position—which is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school—distinguishes based on the tone of the narration. If Quran or Sunnah mention a previous ruling with disapproval (nakir), it is abrogated and not binding. If mentioned neutrally or approvingly, it remains binding. The author then provides concrete examples. Qisas (retaliation) is cited from the Torah, yet it is also prescribed in Islam (Surat al-Ma'idah 5:45), so it remains in effect. The water distribution for Salih's camel is a historical event but demonstrates a principle of fairness. The prohibition of sodomy (liwat) is reaffirmed. In contrast, dietary restrictions on Jews (animals with claws, specific fats) are explicitly stated as punishments in the Quran, and thus they are not binding on Muslims. This nuanced view allows the Hanafi usul to incorporate earlier divine laws while maintaining that the final shari'ah supersedes when explicitly indicated.

Key Terms
شرائع من قبلنا (shara'i' man qablana): Laws revealed to prophets before Prophet Muhammad (saw).
نکیر (nakir): Explicit disapproval or criticism expressed in Quran or Sunnah regarding a previous law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which position on shara'i' man qablana is adopted by the majority (jumhur) according to this passage?
A) Absolutely binding
B) Absolutely non-binding
C) Binding only if mentioned without disapproval
D) Not binding under any circumstance

Key Takeaway
The bindingness of previous prophetic laws depends on whether they are narrated in the Quran or Sunnah without disapproval; if disapproved, they are abrogated.

Taqlid of a Companion: When Is It Obligatory?
Presents different scholarly opinions on the obligation of following a Sahabi's opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between matters that require taqlid of a Sahabi and those that do not according to the Hanafi school, and apply this distinction to new cases.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a Sahabi is binding only when reason cannot reach — the Hanafi school limits its obligation to matters beyond qiyas.

This passage invites us into one of the key methodological debates in usul al-fiqh: the binding nature of a Companion's statement. You will learn the Hanafi stance, the nuance within the school, and the opposing Shafi'i view. The examples sharpen the distinction between matters that qiyas can handle and those that rely on transmitted knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the four opinions presented
Read the passage and list the four positions: preponderant Hanafi, al-Karkhi, al-Shafi'i, and the Hanafi consensus-plus-dispute.
Focus on understanding each position's stance on overriding qiyas.
2
Understand the key distinction: mudrak vs. ghayr mudrak bi-al-qiyas
Matters not accessible to qiyas (ghayr mudrak) are those that cannot be rationally deduced, like specific durations or conditions in worship. For these, taqlid is obligatory by consensus; for mudrak matters, there is disagreement.
This distinction is the central criterion in the Hanafi school.
3
Locate the point of consensus among Hanafis
The text states that Hanafis agree on taqlid of a Sahabi being obligatory in ghayr mudrak matters. In mudrak matters, there is ikhtilaf.
The preponderant view (first opinion) goes further, making taqlid override qiyas even in mudrak matters.
4
Apply the distinction to the given examples
The minimum menstruation period is ghayr mudrak because it is a purely revealed matter; thus Aisha's statement is binding. The transaction example is similarly beyond qiyas.
These examples show how the principle translates into concrete rulings.
5
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i position and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
For the Shafi'i, a Companion's opinion is never binding. The practical consequence: in matters like minimum menstruation, Hanafis accept Aisha's hadith, while Shafi'is may rely on other evidence.
This difference leads to divergent fiqh rulings on the same issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقلید صحابی کا بیان (۱) قول راجح قول تعابی رضی اللہ عنہ کی تقلید واجب ہے اگر وہ خلاف قیاس ہو تو اسکی وجہ سے قیاس کو ترک کر دیا جائے گا۔ قیاس سے غیر صحابی غیر رضی اللہ عنہ کا قیاس مزاد ہے ۔ ایک صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ کا قیاس دوسرے صحابی کے قول سے متروک نہیں ہوگا۔ (۲) امام کرخی رحمۃ اللہ کا قول جو امور غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہیں ان میں قول صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ کی تقلید واجب ہے اور جو مدرک بالقیاس ہوں ان میں قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ (۳) امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا مذھب سنالی رضی اللہ عنہ کی تقلید واجب نہیں خواہ وہ مسئلہ مدرک بالقیاس ہو یا غیر مدرک بالقیاس (۴) احناف کثر الله سواد هم کا مذھب جو اقوال غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہیں ان میں بالاتفاق قول صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ کی تقلید واجب ہے البتہ مدرک بالقیاس میں اختلاف ہے غیر مدرک بالقیاس میں تقلید صحابی کی مثال (۱) اقل مدت حیض کے متعلق حضرت امی عائشہ صدیقہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنھا کا فرمان أقل الحيض للجاريه البكر والتيب ثلثة ايام ولياليها (۳) شراع ما باع باقل مما باع میں حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنھا کا قول ۔ آپ نے اس خاتون سے جس نے حضرت زید بن ارقم رضی اللہ عنہ کے ساتھ شراع ما بات باقل مما بات کا معاملہ کیا
Statement on taqlid of a Companion: (1) The preponderant view: Taqlid of a Companion (may Allah be pleased with him) is obligatory; if it contradicts qiyas, qiyas is abandoned because of it. The qiyas of a non-Companion (may Allah be pleased with him) is inferior [to the Companion's qiyas?]. The qiyas of one Companion will not be abandoned due to the statement of another Companion. (2) The statement of Imam al-Karkhi (may Allah have mercy on him): In matters not accessible to qiyas, taqlid of a Companion is obligatory; in matters accessible to qiyas, qiyas will be followed. (3) The madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him): Taqlid of a Companion is not obligatory, whether the issue is accessible to qiyas or not. (4) The madhhab of the Hanafis (may Allah increase their number): In statements not accessible to qiyas, by consensus, taqlid of a Companion is obligatory; but in matters accessible to qiyas, there is disagreement. Example of taqlid of a Companion in matters not accessible to qiyas: (1) Regarding the minimum duration of menstruation, the statement of Lady Aisha al-Siddiqah (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The minimum menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights.' (3) The statement of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) regarding the transaction 'shira' ma ba'a bi-aqall min ma ba'a' (a sale at less than the original purchase price). She said regarding the woman who made this transaction with Zayd ibn Arqam (may Allah be pleased with him)...
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul al-fiqh issue of taqlid of a Companion (following the opinion of a Sahabi). The text presents four positions: (1) The preponderant Hanafi view holds that a Companion's opinion is binding and can override qiyas, though the qiyas of one Companion is not abandoned for another's opinion. (2) Imam al-Karkhi distinguishes between matters accessible to qiyas (where qiyas is followed) and those not accessible (where the Companion's word is obligatory). (3) Imam al-Shafi'i denies obligation in all cases. (4) The Hanafis (presumably later) agree that in matters beyond qiyas, taqlid is obligatory by consensus, but within qiyas there is disagreement. Examples are given from Aisha's statements on minimum menstruation (which is not accessible to qiyas as it is a pure religious determination) and on a specific transaction (which is also beyond analogical reasoning). The passage highlights the role of Companions' authority in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
تقلید صحابی (taqlid al-sahabi): Following the opinion of a Companion of the Prophet in legal matters.
مدرک بالقیاس (mudrak bi-al-qiyas): A matter that can be known through analogical reasoning (qiyas).
غیر مدرک بالقیاس (ghayr mudrak bi-al-qiyas): A matter that cannot be rationally deduced and must be taken from revelation or Companions' statements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of matters do the Hanafis, by consensus, consider taqlid of a Sahabi obligatory?
A) All legal matters without exception.
B) Matters that are accessible to qiyas (mudrak bi-al-qiyas).
C) Matters that are not accessible to qiyas (ghayr mudrak bi-al-qiyas).
D) Only matters related to worship and ritual purity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates following a Companion's opinion only in matters beyond rational analogy, while matters accessible to qiyas remain debated.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Taqlid al-Sahabi: The Authority of the Companion's Opinion in Hanafi Usul
Explains the ruling on taqlid al-sahabi with positions of major fuqaha and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of taqlid al-sahabi by distinguishing between ghayr mudrak and mudrak bil-qiyas matters and identifying the ikhtilaf among the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A Companion's opinion binds in non-analogical matters; in analogical matters, it is weighed against qiyas.

This passage presents the Hanafi position on the authority of a Companion's statement (taqlid al-sahabi), a debated source of law. You will learn that the binding force depends on whether the issue is 'mudrak bil-qiyas' (derivable by analogy) or not. The text gives specific examples where the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa differed in practice, illustrating the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the preponderant Hanafi view on taqlid al-sahabi: it is wajib when the Companion's statement contradicts qiyas, or when the matter is beyond qiyas.
Note the two conditions: ikhtilaf with qiyas or ghayr mudrak.
2
Classify the matter
Distinguish between ghayr mudrak bil-qiyas (e.g., minimum menstruation) and mudrak bil-qiyas (e.g., salam sale conditions). This classification determines the binding strength of the Companion's opinion.
Use the examples in the passage to solidify this distinction.
3
Trace the ikhtilaf among Hanafis
In mudrak matters, examine how Imam Abu Hanifa (following Ibn Umar) and the Sahibayn (using qiyas) differed on the condition of specifying capital in salam, and on the liability of a common hireling.
Note that the Sahibayn follow a Companion's statement in the hireling case, while Abu Hanifa uses qiyas.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Contrast the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who does not consider taqlid al-sahabi binding in any case.
The thamarah al-khilaf is seen in rulings like the minimum menstruation period.
5
Derive the operative rule
Synthesize: For a mufti, in ghayr mudrak matters taqlid al-sahabi is necessary; in mudrak matters, one may follow either the Companion's statement or qiyas depending on strength of evidence.
This is the practical outcome of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقلید صحابی کا بیان
(۱) قول راجح قول صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ کی تقلید واجب ہے اگر وہ خلاف قیاس ہو تو اس کی وجہ سے قیاس کو ترک کر دیا جائے گا۔ قیاس سے غیر صحابی کا قیاس مراد ہے ۔ ایک صحابی کا قیاس دوسرے صحابی کے قول سے متروک نہیں ہوگا۔
(۲) امام کرخی رحمۃ اللہ کا قول: جو امور غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہیں ان میں قول صحابی کی تقلید واجب ہے اور جو مدرک بالقیاس ہوں ان میں قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔
(۳) امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا مذہب: قول صحابی کی تقلید واجب نہیں خواہ وہ مسئلہ مدرک بالقیاس ہو یا غیر مدرک بالقیاس۔
(۴) احناف کثر الله سوادهم کا مذہب: جو اقوال غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہیں ان میں بالاتفاق قول صحابی کی تقلید واجب ہے البتہ مدرک بالقیاس میں اختلاف ہے۔

غیر مدرک بالقیاس میں تقلید صحابی کی مثال
(۱) اقل مدت حیض کے متعلق حضرت امی عائشہ صدیقہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنھا کا فرمان: أقل الحيض للجارية البكر والتيب ثلاثة أيام ولياليها
(۲) شراع ما باع باقل مما باع میں حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنھا کا قول۔ آپ نے اس خاتون سے جس نے حضرت زید بن ارقم رضی اللہ عنہ کے ساتھ شراع ما باع باقل مما باع کا معاملہ کیا تھا۔ فرمایا: بئس ما شريت و اشتريت۔ اس عورت نے ۸۰۰ درہم میں غلام خریدا تھا اور اس کی قیمت ادا کرنے سے قبل انہی پر ۲۰۰ درھم میں بیچ دیا تھا یہ عمل فریقین میں جائز نہیں۔

غیر مدرک بالقیاس میں مذاہب احناف: بعض احناف یہاں بھی قول صحابی کی تقلید کرتے ہیں اور بعض قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہیں۔

مثال سے وضاحت
بیع سلم میں راس المال کی مقدار بتانا شرط ہے یا نہیں۔ اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ مقدار راس المال کے بیان کو شرط قرار دیتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ اس بارے میں حضرت ابن عمر رضی اللہ عنہ کا ایک قول ملتا ہے جبکہ حضرات صاحبین رحمھما اللہ کے ہاں یہ شرط نہیں وہ قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہیں کہ جب اشارہ کر دیا تو کافی ہے۔ تسمیہ کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ اشارہ تعریف اشیاء میں تسمیہ سے ابلغ ہے۔

اجیر مشترک کا مسئلہ: کہ اگر اس کے پاس اشیاء ضائع ہو جائیں تو اسے ضامن قرار دیا جائے یا نہیں۔ اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ علیہ نے قیاس پر اور صاحبین نے قول صحابی پر عمل کیا ہے۔ صاحبین کے ہاں حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کے قول کی بناء پر ضامن ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ قیاس کرتے ہوئے اسے ضامن نہیں ٹھہراتے کیونکہ یہ امین ہے اور امانت کے ضائع ہونے پر کوئی ضمان نہیں آتا۔ یہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ یہ ضیاع فیما يمكن الاحتراز عنہ کی قبیل سے ہو جیسے چوری اور اگر یہ ضیاع فیما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه کی قبیل سے ہو جیسے بلی جانا تو اختلاف نہیں۔

اجیر مشترک کی مثال دھوبی ( قصار ) ہے۔
Statement of Taqlid of a Companion
(1) The preponderant opinion: Taqlid of the Companion, may Allah be pleased with him, is obligatory. If it contradicts qiyas (analogy), then qiyas is abandoned due to it. By qiyas is meant the qiyas of a non-Companion. The qiyas of one Companion is not abandoned by the statement of another Companion.
(2) The statement of Imam al-Karkhi: In matters not perceptible by qiyas, taqlid of a Companion is obligatory; and in matters perceptible by qiyas, action is taken on qiyas.
(3) The madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i: Taqlid of a Companion is not obligatory, whether the issue is perceptible by qiyas or not.
(4) The madhhab of the Hanafis (may Allah multiply their number): In statements that are not perceptible by qiyas, by consensus taqlid of a Companion is obligatory; but regarding matters perceptible by qiyas, there is disagreement.

Example of taqlid of a Companion in matters not perceptible by qiyas:
(1) Regarding the minimum duration of menstruation, the command of Lady Aisha al-Siddiqa, may Allah be pleased with her: 'The minimum menstruation for the virgin girl and the non-virgin is three days and their nights.'
(2) The statement of Lady Aisha regarding 'Shira' ma ba'a bi-aqall ma ba'a' (buying for less than what one sold). She said to the woman who had entered into a transaction of 'Shira' ma ba'a bi-aqall ma ba'a' with Zayd ibn Arqam, may Allah be pleased with him: 'How bad is that which you bought and sold.' The woman had purchased a slave for 800 dirhams and before paying its price, she sold the same to him for 200 dirhams. This transaction is not permissible between the parties.

Regarding the schools of the Hanafis in matters not perceptible by qiyas: Some Hanafis practice taqlid of a Companion here as well, while others act on qiyas.

Clarification with example:
In salam sale, is mentioning the amount of the capital a condition or not? In this, Imam Abu Hanifa considers the statement of the amount of capital as a condition, because there is a statement of Ibn Umar on this matter. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not consider it a condition; they act on qiyas: when a sign is given, it suffices. Specification is not necessary because the definition of things by sign is more eloquent than specification.

The issue of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak): If goods are lost in his possession, should he be held liable or not? In this, Imam Abu Hanifa acts on qiyas, while the two companions act on the statement of a Companion. According to the two companions, based on the statement of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, he will be liable. Imam Abu Hanifa, using qiyas, does not hold him liable because he is a trustee and no guarantee arises from the loss of a trust. This disagreement is when the loss is of the type that can be guarded against, like theft. But if it is of the type that cannot be guarded against, like a cat going away, then there is no disagreement.

The example of the common hireling is the washerman (qassar).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh discussion on the authority of a Companion's opinion (taqlid al-sahabi). It opens by presenting multiple positions within the madhhab and then provides examples. The Hanafi position is that a Companion's opinion is obligatory to follow in matters that are not amenable to qiyas (non-mudrak bil-qiyas), such as the minimum duration of menstruation, which is known only through revelation and not analogy. In such matters, the Hanafis unanimously accept the Companion's statement as authoritative. However, in matters that can be derived by qiyas, there is internal disagreement among Hanafis: some (like Imam Abu Hanifa in the salam example) prioritize a Companion's statement over qiyas, while others (the Sahibayn) prefer qiyas. The text illustrates this with two fiqh examples: the condition of stating the capital amount in salam sale, and the liability of a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) for loss of goods. In the first, Abu Hanifa follows Ibn Umar's statement requiring specification; the Sahibayn rely on qiyas that a sign suffices. In the second, Abu Hanifa uses qiyas (the hireling is a trustee) and does not impose liability; the Sahibayn follow Ali's statement imposing liability. The passage also records the Shafi'i position that a Companion's opinion is never binding. The overall lesson is that for Hanafis, taqlid al-sahabi is a valid source in non-analogical matters, and in analogical matters it is subject to ijtihad.

Key Terms
تقلید صحابی (taqlid al-sahabi): Following a Companion's opinion in legal rulings, considered wajib in non-qiyas matters by Hanafis.
مدرک بالقیاس (mudrak bil-qiyas): A ruling that can be derived through analogical reasoning (qiyas).
غیر مدرک بالقیاس (ghayr mudrak bil-qiyas): A ruling that cannot be derived through qiyas, such as the minimum duration of menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which type of matters is taqlid al-sahabi (following a Companion's opinion) wajib by consensus?
A) All matters without exception
B) Matters that are mudrak bil-qiyas (perceptible by analogy)
C) Matters that are ghayr mudrak bil-qiyas (not perceptible by analogy)
D) Only in matters where the Companion's statement agrees with qiyas

Key Takeaway
Taqlid al-sahabi is wajib by consensus only in matters beyond qiyas; in qiyas matters, the Hanafi school has internal ikhtilaf and ijtihad may override the Companion's statement.
